## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws express dA/dt as functions of A (zeroth, first, second order, etc.), with possible explicit time dependence arising from integrated coupled kinetics or time-varying external conditions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zeroth-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, first-order reaction)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law kinetics)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis, A catalyzes its own formation with finite capacity)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction with competitive adsorption)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-varying external influence)
- Consecutive reaction (integrated): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (rate from coupled sequential reactions after variable elimination)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order kinetics with background rate)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding or reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates an elementary reaction of order n, where n is typically 0, 1, 2, or 3
- Rational functions of A (numerator/denominator polynomials in A) suggest enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed mechanisms with adsorption-desorption equilibria
- A product term A*(c - A) indicates autocatalytic behavior where the reaction rate peaks at intermediate concentrations
- Explicit time dependence (beyond implicit dependence through A(t)) suggests external forcing, photolysis with varying light, or elimination of intermediate species from a coupled ODE system
- Sum of exponentials in time indicates the system results from analytically solving a linear coupled reaction network
- Negative leading coefficient on A terms indicates consumption/decay of species A, while positive indicates production
- Square root dependence on A (A**0.5) can arise from dissociation equilibria or radical chain mechanisms
- Denominator terms like (1 + c*A)^n arise from quasi-steady-state approximations in catalytic mechanisms with site competition
